href="http://ec.europa.eu">ec<wbr />.europa<wbr />.eu</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:246px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_of_Schuman_Roundabout.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/View_of_Schuman_Roundabout.jpg/244px-View_of_Schuman_Roundabout.jpg" decoding="async" width="244" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/View_of_Schuman_Roundabout.jpg/366px-View_of_Schuman_Roundabout.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/View_of_Schuman_Roundabout.jpg/488px-View_of_Schuman_Roundabout.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2958" data-file-height="1599" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_of_Schuman_Roundabout.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Berlaymont_building" title="Berlaymont building">Berlaymont Building</a>, seat of the European Commission</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>European Commission</b> (<b>EC</b>) is the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive branch</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, responsible for proposing legislation, implementing decisions, upholding the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">EU treaties</a> and managing the day-to-day business of the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_Institutions_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Institutions-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Commissioners swear an oath at the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">European Court of Justice</a> in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg City</a>, pledging to respect the treaties and to be completely independent in carrying out their duties during their mandate.<sup id="cite_ref-oath_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oath-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The Commissioners are proposed by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a>, on the basis of suggestions made by the national governments, and then appointed by the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> after the approval of the European Parliament. It is common, although not a formal requirement, that the commissioners have previously held senior political positions, such as being a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> or a government minister.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">EU institution</a> operates as a <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet government">cabinet government</a>, with 27 <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner" title="European Commissioner">members of the Commission</a> (informally known as "commissioners").<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> There is one member per <a href="/wiki/European_Union_member_state" class="mw-redirect" title="European Union member state">member state</a>, but members are bound by their oath of office to represent the general interest of the EU as a whole rather than their home state.<sup id="cite_ref-oath_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oath-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> One of the 27 is the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">Commission President</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Ursula_von_der_Leyen" title="Ursula von der Leyen">Ursula von der Leyen</a>) proposed by the European Council<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and elected by the European Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-Sch\xc3\xbctze_2012_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sch\xc3\xbctze_2012-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The Council of the European Union then nominates the other members of the Commission in agreement with the nominated President, and the 27 members as a single body are then subject to a vote of approval by the European Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-Article_17:7_TEU_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Article_17:7_TEU-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The current Commission is the <a href="/wiki/Von_der_Leyen_Commission" title="Von der Leyen Commission">Von der Leyen Commission</a>, which took office in December 2019, following the <a href="/wiki/2019_European_Parliament_election" title="2019 European Parliament election">European Parliament elections in May of the same year</a>.\n</p><p>The term <i>Commission</i> is variously used, either in the narrow sense of the 27-member <b>College of Commissioners</b> (or <b>College</b>) or to also include the administrative body of about 32,000 <a href="/wiki/European_Civil_Service" title="European Civil Service">European civil servants</a> who are split into departments called <a href="/wiki/Directorate-General" title="Directorate-General">directorates-general</a> and services.<sup id="cite_ref-rules_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rules-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-staff_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-staff-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The procedural languages of the commission are English, French and German.<sup id="cite_ref-EU_languages_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU_languages-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\nThe Members of the Commission and their "cabinets" (immediate teams) are based in the <a href="/wiki/Berlaymont_building" title="Berlaymont building">Berlaymont building</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Appointment"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Appointment</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Legitimacy_and_criticism"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Legitimacy and criticism</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="toctext">COVID-19 response</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Location"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Commission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_European_Union" title="History of the European Union">History of the European Union</a></div>\n<p>The European Commission derives from one of the five key institutions created in the <a href="/wiki/Supranational_union" title="Supranational union">supranational</a> European Community system, following the proposal of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Schuman" title="Robert Schuman">Robert Schuman</a>, French Foreign Minister, on 9 May 1950. Originating in 1951 as the High Authority in the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a>, the commission has undergone numerous changes in power and composition under various presidents, involving three Communities.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_commission_history_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_commission_history-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment">Establishment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Commission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Establishment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table width="100%" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="1" style="font-size:88%; line-height:1.2em; text-align:center; margin:0">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="text-align:right">Signed<br />In force<br /><a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">Document</a>\n</td>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7; text-align:left">1951<br />1952<br /><b><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1951)" title="Treaty of Paris (1951)">Paris Treaty</a></b>\n</td>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7; text-align:left">1957<br />1958<br /><b><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Rome treaties</a></b>\n</td>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7; text-align:left">1965<br />1967<br /><b><a href="/wiki/Merger_Treaty" title="Merger Treaty">Merger Treaty</a></b>\n</td>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7; text-align:left"><a href="/wiki/Signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Signing of the Treaty of Lisbon">2007</a><br />2009<br /><b><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Lisbon Treaty</a></b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="6">\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7">&#160;\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="background:#42B995; border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7"><a href="/wiki/European_Atomic_Energy_Community" title="European Atomic Energy Community"><span style="color:black;">Commission of the European Atomic Energy Community</span></a>\n</td>\n<td rowspan="3" style="background:#464646; border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7"><a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities"><span style="color:white;">Commission of the European Communities</span></a>\n</td>\n<td rowspan="3" style="background:#192192; border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7"><a class="mw-selflink selflink"><span style="color:white;">European Commission</span></a>\n</td>\n<td rowspan="3" style="background-image: linear-gradient(to right, #192192, white); padding:0">&#160;&#160;\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="background:#93DAE7; border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7"><a href="/wiki/High_Authority_of_the_European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="High Authority of the European Coal and Steel Community"><span style="color:black;">High Authority of the European Coal and Steel Community</span></a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="background:#5FCF4D; border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7"><a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community"><span style="color:black;">Commission of the European Economic Community</span></a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7">&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="border-left:1px solid #C7C7C7"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992953826">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox .navbar{display:block;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox-title .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Structural_evolution_of_the_European_Commission" title="Template:Structural evolution of the European Commission"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Structural_evolution_of_the_European_Commission" title="Template talk:Structural evolution of the European Commission"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Structural_evolution_of_the_European_Commission&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The first Commission originated in 1951 as the nine-member "<a href="/wiki/High_Authority_of_the_European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="High Authority of the European Coal and Steel Community">High Authority</a>" under President <a href="/wiki/Jean_Monnet" title="Jean Monnet">Jean Monnet</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Monnet_Authority" title="Monnet Authority">Monnet Authority</a>). The High Authority was the supranational administrative executive of the new European Coal and Steel Community (ECSC). It took office first on 10 August 1952 in Luxembourg City. In 1958, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaties of Rome</a> had established two new communities alongside the ECSC: the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC) and the <a href="/wiki/European_Atomic_Energy_Community" title="European Atomic Energy Community">European Atomic Energy Community</a> (Euratom). However their executives were called "Commissions" rather than "High Authorities".<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_commission_history_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_commission_history-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The reason for the change in name was the new relationship between the executives and the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council</a>. Some states, such as France, expressed reservations over the power of the High Authority, and wished to limit it by giving more power to the Council rather than the new executives.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_Council_history_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_Council_history-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F028459-0019,_Robert-Schuman-Preis,_Verleihung_an_Walter_Hallstein.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F028459-0019%2C_Robert-Schuman-Preis%2C_Verleihung_an_Walter_Hallstein.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F028459-0019%2C_Robert-Schuman-Preis%2C_Verleihung_an_Walter_Hallstein.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F028459-0019%2C_Robert-Schuman-Preis%2C_Verleihung_an_Walter_Hallstein.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F028459-0019%2C_Robert-Schuman-Preis%2C_Verleihung_an_Walter_Hallstein.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F028459-0019%2C_Robert-Schuman-Preis%2C_Verleihung_an_Walter_Hallstein.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F028459-0019%2C_Robert-Schuman-Preis%2C_Verleihung_an_Walter_Hallstein.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="514" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F028459-0019,_Robert-Schuman-Preis,_Verleihung_an_Walter_Hallstein.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Walter_Hallstein" title="Walter Hallstein">Walter Hallstein</a>, the first President of the Commission</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Louis_Armand" title="Louis Armand">Louis Armand</a> led the <a href="/wiki/Armand_Commission" title="Armand Commission">first Commission of Euratom</a>. <a href="/wiki/Walter_Hallstein" title="Walter Hallstein">Walter Hallstein</a> led the <a href="/wiki/Hallstein_Commission" title="Hallstein Commission">first Commission of the EEC</a>, holding the first formal meeting on 16 January 1958 at the <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_of_Val-Duchesse" title="Ch\xc3\xa2teau of Val-Duchesse">Ch\xc3\xa2teau of Val-Duchesse</a>. It achieved agreement on a contentious cereal price accord, as well as making a positive impression upon third countries when it made its international debut at the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Round" title="Kennedy Round">Kennedy Round</a> of <a href="/wiki/General_Agreement_on_Tariffs_and_Trade" title="General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade">General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade</a> (GATT) negotiations.<sup id="cite_ref-LSE_Chair_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSE_Chair-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Hallstein notably began the consolidation of <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Law of the European Union">European law</a> and started to have a notable impact on national legislation. Little heed was taken of his administration at first but, with help from the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">European Court of Justice</a>, his Commission stamped its authority solidly enough to allow future Commissions to be taken more seriously.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In 1965, however, accumulating differences between the French government of <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> and the other member states on various subjects (British entry, direct elections to Parliament, the <a href="/wiki/Fouchet_Plan" title="Fouchet Plan">Fouchet Plan</a> and the budget) triggered the <a href="/wiki/Empty_chair_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Empty chair crisis">"empty chair" crisis</a>, ostensibly over proposals for the <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a>. Although the institutional crisis was solved the following year, it cost <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Hirsch" title="\xc3\x89tienne Hirsch">\xc3\x89tienne Hirsch</a> his presidency of <a href="/wiki/Euratom" class="mw-redirect" title="Euratom">Euratom</a> and later Walter Hallstein the EEC presidency, despite his otherwise being viewed as the most \'dynamic\' leader until <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Delors" title="Jacques Delors">Jacques Delors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LSE_Chair_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSE_Chair-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_development">Early development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Commission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1013635363">.mw-parser-output .sidebar{width:22em;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 1em;background:#f8f9fa;border:1px solid href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven" title="Group of Seven">G7</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below">\n<a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Europe.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of Europe.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/32px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="21" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/48px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/64px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="540" /></a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Portal:European_Union" title="Portal:European Union">European Union&#32;portal</a> <div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_political_science#Politics_by_region" title="Outline of political science">Other countries</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r992953826"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Template:Politics of the European Union"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Template talk:Politics of the European Union"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The three bodies, collectively named the <b>European Executives</b>, co-existed until 1 July 1967 when, under the <a href="/wiki/Merger_Treaty" title="Merger Treaty">Merger Treaty</a>, they were combined into a single administration under President <a href="/wiki/Jean_Rey_(politician)" title="Jean Rey (politician)">Jean Rey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_commission_history_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_commission_history-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Owing to the merger, the <a href="/wiki/Rey_Commission" title="Rey Commission">Rey Commission</a> saw a temporary increase to 14 members\xe2\x80\x94although subsequent Commissions were reduced back to nine, following the formula of one member for small states and two for larger states.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_composition_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_composition-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The Rey Commission completed the Community\'s <a href="/wiki/Customs_union" title="Customs union">customs union</a> in 1968, and campaigned for a more powerful, elected, <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Meet_Rey_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meet_Rey-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Despite Rey being the first President of the combined communities, Hallstein is seen as the first President of the modern Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_commission_history_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_commission_history-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Malfatti_Commission" title="Malfatti Commission">Malfatti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mansholt_Commission" title="Mansholt Commission">Mansholt Commissions</a> followed with work on monetary co-operation and the first <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">enlargement</a> to the north in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-Meet_Mansholt_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meet_Mansholt-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Meet_Malfatti_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meet_Malfatti-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> With that enlargement, the College of Commissioners membership increased to thirteen under the <a href="/wiki/Ortoli_Commission" title="Ortoli Commission">Ortoli Commission</a> (the United Kingdom as a large member was granted two Commissioners), which dealt with the enlarged community during economic and international instability at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_composition_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_composition-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Meet_Ortoli_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meet_Ortoli-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The external representation of the Community took a step forward when President <a href="/wiki/Roy_Jenkins" title="Roy Jenkins">Roy Jenkins</a>, recruited to the presidency in January 1977 from his role as <a href="/wiki/Home_Secretary" title="Home Secretary">Home Secretary</a> of the United Kingdom\'s <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> government,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> became the first President to attend a <a href="/wiki/G8" class="mw-redirect" title="G8">G8</a> summit on behalf of the Community.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Jenkins_Commission_(EU)" title="Jenkins Commission (EU)">Jenkins Commission</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaston_Thorn" title="Gaston Thorn">Gaston Thorn</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Thorn_Commission" title="Thorn Commission">Commission</a> oversaw the Community\'s enlargement to the south, in addition to beginning work on the <a href="/wiki/Single_European_Act" title="Single European Act">Single European Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Meet_Thorn_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meet_Thorn-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jacques_Delors">Jacques Delors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Commission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Jacques Delors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078267-0023,_Bonn,_Ministerpr%C3%A4sidenten_mit_EU-Kommissar_Delors-CROPPED.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078267-0023%2C_Bonn%2C_Ministerpr%C3%A4sidenten_mit_EU-Kommissar_Delors-CROPPED.jpg/170px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078267-0023%2C_Bonn%2C_Ministerpr%C3%A4sidenten_mit_EU-Kommissar_Delors-CROPPED.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e4/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078267-0023%2C_Bonn%2C_Ministerpr%C3%A4sidenten_mit_EU-Kommissar_Delors-CROPPED.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="173" data-file-height="243" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078267-0023,_Bonn,_Ministerpr%C3%A4sidenten_mit_EU-Kommissar_Delors-CROPPED.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Delors" title="Jacques Delors">Delors</a>, one of the most notable presidents in the commission\'s history</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Delors_Commission" title="Delors Commission">Delors Commission</a></div>\n<p>The Commission headed by Jacques Delors was seen as giving the Community a sense of direction and dynamism.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Delors and his College are also considered as the "<a href="/wiki/Founding_father" class="mw-redirect" title="Founding father">founding fathers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Meet_Delors_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meet_Delors-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/International_Herald_Tribune" title="International Herald Tribune">International Herald Tribune</a></i> noted the work of Delors at the end of his second term in 1992: "Mr. Delors rescued the European Community from the doldrums. He arrived when Europessimism was at its worst. Although he was a little-known former French finance minister, he breathed life and hope into the EC and into the dispirited Brussels Commission. In his first term, from 1985 to 1988, he rallied Europe to the call of the single market, and when appointed to a second term he began urging Europeans toward the far more ambitious goals of economic, monetary and political union".<sup id="cite_ref-IHT_Delors_quote_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHT_Delors_quote-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jacques_Santer">Jacques Santer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Commission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Jacques Santer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Santer_Commission" title="Santer Commission">Santer Commission</a></div>\n<p>The successor to Delors was <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Santer" title="Jacques Santer">Jacques Santer</a>. As a result of a fraud and corruption scandal, the entire Santer Commission was forced by the Parliament to resign in 1999; a central role was played by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89dith_Cresson" title="\xc3\x89dith Cresson">\xc3\x89dith Cresson</a>. These frauds were revealed by an internal auditor, <a href="/wiki/Paul_van_Buitenen" title="Paul van Buitenen">Paul van Buitenen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>That was the first time a College of Commissioners had been forced to resign <i>en masse</i>, and represented a shift of power towards the Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> However, the Santer Commission did carry out work on the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amsterdam" title="Treaty of Amsterdam">Treaty of Amsterdam</a> and the euro.<sup id="cite_ref-Meet_Santer_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meet_Santer-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In response to the scandal, the <a href="/wiki/European_Anti-Fraud_Office" title="European Anti-Fraud Office">European Anti-Fraud Office</a> (OLAF) was created.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romano_Prodi">Romano Prodi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Commission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Romano Prodi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Prodi_Commission" title="Prodi Commission">Prodi Commission</a></div>\n<p>Following Santer, <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a> took office. The Amsterdam Treaty had increased the commission\'s powers and Prodi was dubbed by the press as something akin to a Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Powers were strengthened again; the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nice" title="Treaty of Nice">Treaty of Nice</a>, signed in 2001, gave the Presidents more power over the composition of the College of Commissioners.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_commission_history_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_commission_history-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Jos.C3.A9_Manuel_Barroso"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Jos\xc3\xa9_Manuel_Barroso">Jos\xc3\xa9 Manuel Barroso</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Commission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Jos\xc3\xa9 Manuel Barroso">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Barroso_Commission" title="Barroso Commission">Barroso Commission</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Manuel Barroso">Jos\xc3\xa9 Manuel Barroso</a> became president in 2004: the Parliament once again asserted itself in objecting to the proposed membership of the Barroso Commission. Owing to this opposition, Barroso was forced to reshuffle his College before taking office.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The Barroso Commission was also the first full Commission since the enlargement in 2004 to 25 members; hence, the number of Commissioners at the end of the Prodi Commission had reached 30. As a result of the increase in the number of states, the Amsterdam Treaty triggered a reduction in the number of Commissioners to one per state, rather than two for the larger states.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_composition_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_composition-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Allegations of fraud and corruption were again raised in 2004 by former chief auditor Jules Muis.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> A Commission officer, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Guido_Strack&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Guido Strack (page does not exist)">Guido Strack</a>, reported alleged fraud and abuses in his department in the years 2002\xe2\x80\x932004 to OLAF, and was fired as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, Paul van Buitenen (the former auditor known from the Santer Commission scandal) accused the European Anti-Fraud Office (OLAF) of a lack of independence and effectiveness.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Barroso\'s first Commission term expired on 31 October 2009. Under the Treaty of Nice, the first Commission to be appointed after the number of member states reached 27 would have to be reduced to "less than the number of Member States". The exact number of Commissioners was to be decided by a unanimous vote of the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>, and membership would rotate equally between member states. Following the <a href="/wiki/2007_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2007 enlargement of the European Union">accession of Romania and Bulgaria</a> in January 2007, this clause took effect for the next Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The Treaty of Lisbon, which came into force on 1 December 2009, mandated a reduction of the number of commissioners to two-thirds of member-states from 2014 unless the Council decided otherwise. Membership would rotate equally and no member state would have more than one Commissioner. However, the treaty was rejected by voters in Ireland in 2008 with one main concern being the loss of their Commissioner. Hence a guarantee given for a rerun of the vote was that the council would use its power to amend the number of Commissioners upwards. However, according to the treaties it still has to be fewer than the total number of members, thus it was proposed that the member state that does not get a Commissioner would get the post of High Representative&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 the so-called 26+1 formula.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> This guarantee (which may find its way into the next treaty amendment, probably in an accession treaty) contributed to the Irish approving the treaty in a second referendum in 2009.\n</p><p>Lisbon also combined the posts of <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_External_Relations" title="European Commissioner for External Relations">European Commissioner for External Relations</a> with the council\'s <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">High Representative for the Common Foreign and Security Policy</a>. This post, also a <a href="/wiki/Vice-President_of_the_European_Commission" title="Vice-President of the European Commission">Vice-President of the Commission</a>, would chair the Council of the European Union\'s foreign affairs meetings as well as the commission\'s external relations duties.<sup id="cite_ref-Europa_web_portal_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_web_portal-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The treaty further provides that the most recent European elections should be "<i>taken into account</i>" when appointing the President of the European Commission, and although they are still proposed by the European Council; the European Parliament "<i>elects</i>" candidates to the office, rather than "<i>approves</i>" them as under the Treaty of Nice.<sup id="cite_ref-Article_17:7_TEU_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Article_17:7_TEU-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Europa_web_portal_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_web_portal-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jean-Claude_Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Commission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Jean-Claude Juncker">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Juncker_Commission" title="Juncker Commission">Juncker Commission</a></div>\n<p>In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a> became President of the European Commission.\n</p><p>Juncker appointed his previous campaign director and head of the transition team, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Selmayr" title="Martin Selmayr">Martin Selmayr</a>, as his chief of cabinet. During the Juncker presidency Selmayr has been described as "the most powerful EU chief of staff ever."<sup id="cite_ref-politico_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-politico-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ursula_von_der_Leyen">Ursula von der Leyen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Commission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ursula von der Leyen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:(Ursula_von_der_Leyen)_2019.07.16._Ursula_von_der_Leyen_presents_her_vision_to_MEPs_2_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/%28Ursula_von_der_Leyen%29_2019.07.16._Ursula_von_der_Leyen_presents_her_vision_to_MEPs_2_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-%28Ursula_von_der_Leyen%29_2019.07.16._Ursula_von_der_Leyen_presents_her_vision_to_MEPs_2_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/%28Ursula_von_der_Leyen%29_2019.07.16._Ursula_von_der_Leyen_presents_her_vision_to_MEPs_2_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-%28Ursula_von_der_Leyen%29_2019.07.16._Ursula_von_der_Leyen_presents_her_vision_to_MEPs_2_%28cropped%29.jpg
